<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-staging">Clinical Staging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-staging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt; Stage 0- This is either pre-invasive carcinoma or carcinoma in situ. This stage precedes the development of many cases of invasive carcinoma.</p>
<p>It is asymptomatic and can only be discovered by a cervical smears and biopsies.</p>
<p>The tumour is confined to the cervical epithelium.</p>
<p>&gt; Stage 1a- the tumour has spread/invasion is 3mm deep. =1b- Spreads greater than 3mm deep
&gt; Stage 2a- The tumour has extended beyond the cervix, Spreads beyond cervix, and upper 2/3s of vagina.
&gt; 2b- Extends into the parametrium but does not reach the lateral pelvic walls. (spread into tissues next to the cervix)-parametria.
&gt; Stage 3a- Spread/tumour involves lower 1/3 of the vagina.
&gt; Stage-3b- The tumour involves lateral walls of the pelvis and/or blocking 1/both ureters (hydronephrosis)
&gt; Stage 4a- Involves neighbouring/surrounding organ like the bladder &amp;rectum.
&gt; Stage 4b- distant metastasis to organs like the lungs, brain, liver and bones.
&gt; Staging is important as it helps in making decision of the method of treatment.
&gt; For effective staging, thorough pelvic examination-swollen L/nodes, &amp; other investigations like ct-scan, CXR, MRI, Cystoscopy, Protoscopy, hysteroscopy etc are carried out.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Treatments of cervical tumours/carcinomas depend on the stage of the disease and the gestation if the woman is pregnant. Methods of managing cancer includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Simple &amp; extensive surgeries/ operations.</li>
<li>Medical- chemotherapy</li>
<li>Radiotherapy- both internal &amp; external</li>
<li>Combined therapy</li>
<li>Palliative care.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Stage 0 to 1a= The following models of management can be used.(carcinoma in tissue)</li>
<li>Laser therapy- where a laser is used to burn away any abnormal cells.</li>
<li>Cryotherapy/surgery- a cold probe is used to freeze abnormal cells with the help of liquid nitrogen after colposcopy.</li>
<li>Cauterization- The burning of the abnormal cells.</li>
<li>Loop electrical excisional surgical procedure (LEEP)-Loop diathermy and Cone biopsy are used.</li>
<li>In stage 1b to 2a or for invasive carcinoma-Simple or radicle hysterectomy is the most commonly recommended surgical procedures for treating stages 1 and 2 of Ca cervix.</li>
<li>Radicle hysterectomy – Is the removal of the whole uterus, supporting tissues, pelvic nodes, and distal vagina.</li>
<li>Radicle hysterectomy is combined with bilateral salpingectomy and oophrectomy. To clear all cancerous cells.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="radiotherapy">Radiotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This involves the use of radium or radiations to kill or destroy cancer cells. It consists of external beam irradiations &amp; intracavity implants. The intracavity implants are usually left in place between 24-72 hours.</li>
<li>From stage 1b to 4- surgery, radiotherapy or a combination of both can be used to manage cancer.</li>
<li>Patients who have been treated well with surgery might be given radiotherapy with or without chemotherapy in order to clear all cancer cells and to reduce the risks of re-ocurance/relapse.</li>
<li>Note that treatment options in cancer mainly depend on the size of the tumour (staging), age of the patient, and if one will become pregnant some day.</li>
<li>If pregnancy will be desired then simple surgical procedures will be done to preserve the uterus depending on the stage of the tumour.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemotherapy">CHEMOTHERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Chemotherapy can be combined with radiotherapy to try &amp; cure cancer. Or it can be used still in combination or as a sole palliative Rx for advanced stage 3&amp;4 of cervical cancer to slow the progression of the tumour &amp; relieve symptoms.</p>
<p>&gt; Chemo involves the use of a single drug called cisplatin therapy, or a combination of different chemotherapy drugs. Anti-cancerous drugs commonly used include:-
&gt; Vincristine, cyclophosphamide, Methotraxate, Bleomycin,</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Primary prevention;-</li>
<li>Discourage early sexual intercourse.</li>
<li>Encourage male circumcision and teach male partners proper hygiene to remove smegma.</li>
<li>Visual inspection of the cervix under acetic acid 6weeks after delivery.</li>
<li>Annual screening for all women of child bearing age or those who are sexually active.</li>
<li>Prevention and prompt treatment of sexually transmitted infections.</li>
<li>Continuous health education on how the cancer spreads and its risk factors, and dangers- increase community awareness on prevention.</li>
<li>Avoid early marriages by emphasizing education of the girl child.</li>
<li>Behaviour change- avoiding alcoholism and drug abuse</li>
<li>Vaccination of all sexually active women with HPV vaccines-Bivalent HPV-16/18 vaccines (cervirax).</li>
<li>Quadrivalent HPV-6/11/16/18 vaccine.</li>
<li>Secondary prevention: - involves pap smear screening and prompt treatment of identified pre-invasive lesions or cervical intraepithelial neoplasia.</li>
</ul>
